- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: engineers who know the sections separately improvise the close under deadline, running commands but skipping the sweep, or affirming the checklist from memory, the partial closes that let section 6's rejections ship

- **revision_decision:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to anchor the section on the full-close walkthrough plus one failure drill, hand the learner a change that passes all four commands while violating two rejections, layering leakage and missing cancellation validation, and require the sweep to catch both
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the failure drill teaches the file's central lesson mechanically, the command gate is necessary and insufficient, feeling a green battery coexist with two real rejections converts the sweep from ceremony into the half of the gate that catches what machines cannot

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed symbol-count boundary misprices gate work, whose real units are per-close cost, the fixed command-battery-plus-sweep price every handoff pays, per-waiver cost when a local convention needs a recorded departure, and per-escalation cost when risk classification triggers the advanced pair
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because closing cost is dominated by the fixed unit, the battery runs in machine time and the sweep in bounded reviewer time, so gate workload scales with handoff frequency, not change size, small frequent changes pay the close more often than large rare ones
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: pricing gates per symbol invites batching, teams accumulate giant changes to amortize closes, exactly backwards, large closes make sweeps shallower and defect attribution harder, the fixed cost should push toward smaller closes, not fewer
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: budgeting closing work under this theme, implementation workload lives with the reliability theme's surface units
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to restate the model in three units, fixed close cost per handoff, waiver cost per recorded departure, escalation cost per high-risk classification
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that automating the fixed unit changes team behavior more than its own cost suggests, when the battery and record generation run unattended, the marginal close cost drops to sweep time alone, removing the amortization pressure that produces oversized changes, gate automation is really batch-size policy

## Section 019: Reliability Target
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed document-property thresholds stand where closing invariants should, every release claim backed by a complete gate record, zero releases with a failed-or-skipped required command, every local-convention departure carrying a recorded waiver, and every high-risk close showing its advanced-gate results
- **supporting_reason:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because each target restates a file mechanism as an invariant, the record target operationalizes run and require success, the waiver target holds the two-authority split, and the escalation target keeps the optional pair from decaying into never
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: targets held informally decay at deadlines, the first skipped sweep under pressure normalizes the second, and gate discipline is precisely the discipline that deadline pressure tests
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: closing invariants for work under this theme, code-level invariants live with the reliability theme's targets
- **revision_decision:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to publish the four targets with evidence methods, release audit for records, CI enforcement for commands, review sampling for waivers, and record inspection for escalations
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the command target is the only one enforceable purely by machine, branch protection requiring the four checks makes skipping structurally impossible, so wiring it first converts the most deadline-vulnerable target into the most deadline-proof one, exactly where the protection is needed
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to wire the command target into branch protection and hold the three record-based targets through release audit
- **supporting_reason:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because each target restates a file mechanism as an invariant, the record target operationalizes run and require success, the waiver target holds the two-authority split, and the escalation target keeps the optional pair from decaying into never

- **revision_decision:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: publish the four targets with evidence methods, release audit for records, CI enforcement for commands, review sampling for waivers, and record inspection for escalations

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed corpus-process bullets stand where closing-gate retry doctrine should, a failed required command is a fix-forward signal, never a rerun-until-green candidate, because all four commands are deterministic on identical inputs, and any command that flakes is reporting environment debt, not test luck
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because fmt, clippy, and build are pure functions of source and toolchain, and the test command inherits whatever determinism the suite provides, so gate retries can only launder nondeterminism that some upstream discipline, usually test isolation, has already failed to provide
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: retry-until-green on the gate teaches the team the badge lies, each laundered flake ships with a green record that certifies less than it claims, the gate equivalent of the checklist rot the failure table names
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: retry semantics for this theme's gate battery, suite-level flake doctrine lives with the testing themes and code-level retry design with the reliability theme
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add the gate regime, zero automatic retries on the four required commands, deterministic failures fix forward, nondeterministic failures route to the owning suite's quarantine process before the close proceeds
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that backpressure at the gate is release-shaped, when closes start failing repeatedly the correct response is to stop opening new work and repay whatever debt the failures report, toolchain drift, suite flakes, feature-matrix breakage, a red gate is the system's only structural veto over more work-in-progress

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed task-splitting bounds stand beside the file's real scale seams, the command gate assumes one workspace where all features build together, the checklist assumes requirements traceable in one bundle format, and the close assumes one team owning the release, each assumption breaks at a nameable size
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because multi-workspace monorepos break the single battery invocation, cross-team releases break single-owner records, and polyglot or multi-bundle codebases break the requirement-linkage item's format assumption, the file's mechanisms are single-context by construction
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: stretching a single close across contexts produces the worst artifact, one gate record signing for workspaces its commands never ran against, completeness theater at exactly the scale where verification matters most
